<Construct>
To solve a time calculation problem, follow these steps:
1. Convert the times to a 24-hour format if necessary.
2. Subtract the earlier time from the later time.
3. If the minutes of the earlier time are greater than the minutes of the later time, borrow 1 hour from the later time and add 60 minutes to it.
4. Subtract the minutes and then the hours.
</Construct>
<Subject>Time Calculation</Subject>
<Question>
What is the difference between 10:45 AM and 1:30 PM?
</Question>
<Incorrect Answer>2 hours and 45 minutes</Incorrect Answer>
<Misconception>Does not subtract from the hours, when having to borrow for a time calculation</Misconception>

<Construct>When determining the time after a certain number of hours, make sure to consider whether it is in the morning or afternoon.</Construct>
<Subject>Time Calculation</Subject>
<Question>
If it is 9:00 AM now, what time will it be 15 hours later?
</Question>
<Incorrect Answer>6:00 PM</Incorrect Answer>
<Misconception>Confuses AM and PM when calculating time</Misconception>

<Misconception>Given the length of the sides, still does not recognise there is enough information to find the area</Misconception>

<Misconception>
When multiplying a decimal by a power of 10, just adds a zero to the end of the number, not changing the place value of the digits
</Misconception>

<Incorrect Answer>2^6</Incorrect Answer>
<Misconception>Believes that when multiplying a number with a power, the multiplier is added onto the power</Misconception>

```xml
</Misconception>
```

</Incorrect Answer>
<Misconception>Includes too many possibilities when given an 'at least' question in probability</Misconception>

<Construct>
To solve a quadratic equation, follow these steps:
Step 1: Write the equation in the standard form ax^2 + bx + c = 0.
Step 2: Calculate the discriminant b^2 - 4ac.
Step 3: If the discriminant is negative, the equation has no real solutions.
</Construct>
<Subject>Quadratic Equations</Subject>
<Question>
Solve the equation x^2 - 2x + 3 = 0.
</Question>
<Incorrect Answer>0</Incorrect Answer>
<Misconception>Gives an answer of 0 when there are no solutions to an equation.</Misconception>

<Construct>
To find the median of a set of numbers, first arrange the numbers in ascending order. If the number of observations is odd, the median is the middle number. If the number of observations is even, the median is the average of the two middle numbers.
</Construct>
<Subject>Median Calculation</Subject>
<Question>
What is the median of the following dataset: -5, -3, 0, 2, 4?
</Question>
<Incorrect Answer>We cannot calculate the median because the dataset contains negative numbers.</Incorrect Answer>
<Misconception>Believes that we cannot calculate the median of a dataset that contains negative numbers</Misconception>

<Construct>
```
To find the nth term of an arithmetic sequence, you use the formula \( a_n = a_1 + (n-1)d \), where \( a_1 \) is the first term, \( d \) is the common difference, and \( n \) is the term number.
</Construct>
<Subject>
Arithmetic Sequences
</Subject>
<Question>
What is the 5th term of the arithmetic sequence with first term 3 and common difference 4?
</Question>
<Incorrect Answer>
23
</Incorrect Answer>
<Misconception>
Uses difference as index instead of coefficient in nth term rule
</Misconception>
```

<Construct>

</Construct>

</Subject>

</Question>
<Incorrect Answer>

</Incorrect Answer>

<Construct>
To find the quartiles of a dataset, we first need to arrange the data in ascending order. Then, we divide the data into four equal parts. The first quartile (Q1) is the median of the first half of the data, the second quartile (Q2) is the median of the entire data, and the third quartile (Q3) is the median of the second half of the data.
</Construct>
<Subject>Statistics</Subject>
<Question>
Given the dataset: 6, 7, 15, 36, 39, 40, 41, 42, 43, 47, 49, find the first quartile (Q1).
</Question>
<Incorrect Answer>
Q1 = 15
</Incorrect Answer>
<Misconception>Believes quartiles are at 1/4 and 3/4 through the range of the data</Misconception>

<Construct>Explain how to use the capture-recapture method</Construct>

```
<Incorrect Answer>
The probability is (3/5) * (1/4).
</Incorrect Answer>
<Misconception>
Believes you always reduce the numerator and denominator by 1 when writing the probability for a second pick without replacement on a tree diagram.
</Misconception>
```
